--- THINKING ---
**Analyzing Regex Grouping**

I've discovered the regex is matching option lists across multiple questions on a page. The Moodle split feature groups multiple questions, causing overlap. I need to refine the regex to isolate options more precisely, addressing this grouping behavior. The focus is now on improving the accuracy of option detection in this particular context.


**Investigating Question Separation**

I'm now focusing on separating questions correctly, especially when multiple questions appear on the same page. It seems Moodle combines questions with headers like "Question 2" and "Question 3" in close proximity. The problem is I'm trying to split based on "Question \d+", which seems to work, but is incomplete. The question text and options can appear later on the same page. Now, I need to account for this text layout to capture each question block completely, avoiding missing question data, as seen with "Question 2" on page 2. I'm checking the source PDF text to confirm.


**Isolating Question Bodies**

I've realized the key is isolating complete "question bodies." These are blocks of text containing the question, its options (a, b, c, d...), and the correct answer feedback. Regardless of page layout or header order, the bodies are contiguous. I can parse a question by finding the correct answer feedback and backtracing to the options and question text. This appears far more reliable than parsing based on the headers.


**Implementing Backtracking Parsing**

I'm now fully committed to the backtracking parser strategy. I'm focusing on the structural components: finding the correct answer lines and tracing back to locate questions and options. I'm building a Python script, `parse_pdf_to_json.py`, with refined logic, especially for the option extraction, by matching lines with `a.`, `b.`, `c.`, `d.` etc. The key here is precisely identifying the start and end of the options list before the correct answers. Next, I'll identify how to find the answer indices within the options! The logic also handles multi-select questions via answer plurality. I'll test it using `Exam__SS2023.pdf`.

**Analyzing Question Integration**

I've made a breakthrough! The sample question is drawing options from both Question 1 and Question 2. My initial hypothesis is confirmed – the backtracking process is grabbing options from both questions simultaneously because they're interwoven in the text. **Refining Option Identification**

I've hit on a simpler, more elegant method for identifying options! It boils down to backtracking from the correct answer line. I'm looking for option lines (d., c., b., a.) in reverse order. The crucial thing? I stop once I hit an "a." (or "a)") because that signals the beginning of the *current* question's options. Any lines above that "a." belong to a previous question. This looks incredibly promising. I'm eager to verify this!

2. To run the React component locally in VS Code:

**1. Create a new React app**
```bash
npx create-react-app ml-quiz
cd ml-quiz
```

**2. Replace the default App**

Delete `src/App.js` and save the downloaded `ml_quiz.jsx` file as `src/App.js`. Remove the import line at the top (`import { useState } from "react"` is fine, but remove the `export default` — actually keep everything, just rename the file).

Actually the easiest way: just copy the entire content of `ml_quiz.jsx` into `src/App.js`.

**3. Run it**
```bash
npm start
```

That's it — it opens automatically at `http://localhost:3000`.

---

**VS Code tips:**
- Install the **ES7+ React/Redux/React-Native snippets** extension for syntax highlighting
- Install **Prettier** for auto-formatting

**If you get an error** about JSX, make sure the file is saved as `.jsx` or `.js` — both work with Create React App.

**Question 1** (page 1): True/False about binary search trees — Student selected (b) False. *This is about BST property.*

**Question 2** (page 2): Binary Search Tree — Find value at index 3 after inserting and removing. MCQ with options. Student selected (c) 15.

**Question 3** (page 3): Topological sort — which is NOT a valid topological order. MCQ. Student selected (b).

**Question 4** (page 3): Depth-first search starting from node A — find value at index 2 of DFS result. Student selected (d) D.

**Question 5** (page 4): Open-answer — Boyer-Moore last function for "banana" pattern. This is a table-fill question.

**Question 6** (page 5): Open-answer — Master Theorem recurrence T(N) = 2T(N/2) + N.

**Question 7** (page 6): MCQ — Time complexity of code. Student selected (b) O(f^2).

**Question 8** (page 7): MCQ — Min-heap removemin() 3 times, find element at index 9. Student selected (a) 13.

**Question 9** (pages 8-9): Open-answer — MaxHeap bottom-up building.

**Question 10** (page 10): Open-answer — BucketSort.

**Question 11** (page 11): MCQ — Recursive function output for n=6. Student selected (e) 48.

**Question 12** (page 12): MCQ — Queue vs Stack difference. Student selected (c).

I'll convert the MCQ questions (Q1-Q4, Q7-Q8, Q11-Q12) to the quiz format. For open-answer questions (Q5, Q6, Q9, Q10), I'll convert them into MCQ format with the correct answer included.

Let me first verify correctness of a few answers by computing them:

**Q11 - Rec_function(6):**
- Rec_function(6): 6 is even → 6 * Rec_function(4)
- Rec_function(4): 4 is even → 4 * Rec_function(2)
- Rec_function(2): 2 is even → 2 * Rec_function(0)
- Rec_function(0): return 1
- So: 2*1=2, 4*2=8, 6*8=48 ✓ Answer is (e) 48

**Q7 - Time complexity:** The code has a for loop O(f²) and a while loop O(f²). Total O(f²). ✓ Answer is (b) O(f²)
